  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_289b33fe-94db-4071-b120-1e19fb65bbc9'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer2524889032412188876">Goodreads Choice Award Nominee for Debut Goodreads Author <br/> <br/>Daniel Mulligan is tough, snarky, and tattooed, hiding his self-consciousness behind sarcasm.   <span id="freeText2524889032412188876" style="display:none">Goodreads Choice Award Nominee for Debut Goodreads Author <br /> <br />Daniel Mulligan is tough, snarky, and tattooed, hiding his self-consciousness behind sarcasm. Daniel has never fit in—not at home in Philadelphia with his auto mechanic father and brothers, and not at school where his Ivy League classmates looked down on him. Now, Daniel’s relieved to have a job at a small college in Holiday, Northern Michigan, but he’s a city boy through and through, and it’s clear that this small town is one more place he won’t fit in. <br /> <br />Rex Vale clings to routine to keep loneliness at bay: honing his muscular body, perfecting his recipes, and making custom furniture. Rex has lived in Holiday for years, but his shyness and imposing size have kept him from connecting with people. <br /> <br />When the two men meet, their chemistry is explosive, but Rex fears Daniel will be another in a long line of people to leave him, and Daniel has learned that letting anyone in can be a fatal weakness. Just as they begin to break down the walls keeping them apart, Daniel is called home to Philadelphia, where he discovers a secret that changes the way he understands everything. <br /> <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6090518621064854356"><b>2 <i>um</i> stars. DNF @40%. Review posted July 13, 2015</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436627157ra/15486108.gif' alt=' photo oie_gIiJDxJS4Rwr_zpssgzleuym.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436627157ra/15486109.gif' alt=' photo oie_0zlpMvMPcJia_zps9qcmcls3.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>120 x um</b><br/><br/><i>"I, um."<br/><br/>"Um," I say.<br/><br/>"Um," I mumble.<br/><br/>"Oh, um, I--"<br/><br/>"Um, yeah."<br/><br/>"Changing the subject: check. Um, he's…Well, he's…"<br/><br/>"Like Marilyn Monroe--she just, um--you know, she was a little banged up,…<br/><br/>Um…<br/><br/>"Um, yeah, I'll see you," I say.<br/><br/>"Um. Good night."<br/><br/>"Um, I mean…"<br/><br/>"Um, just--in my shoe--or…"<br/><br/>"Um, so, yeah. It's not hard to replace them," I say to Paul.<br/><br/>"I, um, I--did you fix my desk?"<br/><br/>"Um, I'm sorry, Bernard, what was that?"<br/><br/>"Um, well, …"<br/><br/>"Um. Is that true?"<br/><br/>"U</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6090518621064854356" style="display:none"><b>2 <i>um</i> stars. DNF @40%. Review posted July 13, 2015</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436627157ra/15486108.gif" alt=" photo oie_gIiJDxJS4Rwr_zpssgzleuym.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436627157ra/15486109.gif" alt=" photo oie_0zlpMvMPcJia_zps9qcmcls3.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>120 x um</b><br><br><i>"I, um."<br><br>"Um," I say.<br><br>"Um," I mumble.<br><br>"Oh, um, I--"<br><br>"Um, yeah."<br><br>"Changing the subject: check. Um, he's…Well, he's…"<br><br>"Like Marilyn Monroe--she just, um--you know, she was a little banged up,…<br><br>Um…<br><br>"Um, yeah, I'll see you," I say.<br><br>"Um. Good night."<br><br>"Um, I mean…"<br><br>"Um, just--in my shoe--or…"<br><br>"Um, so, yeah. It's not hard to replace them," I say to Paul.<br><br>"I, um, I--did you fix my desk?"<br><br>"Um, I'm sorry, Bernard, what was that?"<br><br>"Um, well, …"<br><br>"Um. Is that true?"<br><br>"Um, you didn't did you?"<br><br>"Thanks. Um, should we go?"<br><br>"Um, I should--here, let me do the dishes since you cooked…."<br><br>"Um, my rage at the world was not cute," I insist...<br><br>"Um. Yeah.<br>"Do you tell Ginger everything?"<br>"Um. No," I say, completely lost in his eyes. He focuses on me like nothing I've ever experienced, like he's reading every blink and breath.<br><br>"Um," he says, "I'm not so good with computers."<br><br>"Um. Breakfast?"</i><br><br>etc.<br><br>Saying that all those <i>ums</i> annoyed the living daylights out of me doesn't even begin to cover it!<br><br><u>He has a PhD in English for Pete's sake and…um…like…okay. Okay?</u><br><br><i>Um</i> seems to be highly contagious.<br><br>Not only Daniel said <i>um,</i> even Rex and the secondary characters had a tendency to use that I-don't-know-what-to-say-so-I-use-the-filler-um word.<br><br>I quote Daniel:<br><br><b>
  <i>Yeah, Rex, can I have your phone number in case you ever want to talk to a socially awkward idiot?</i>
</b><br><br><br><u>Smiling, laughing or grinning</u><br><br>123 x smile, smiles, smiled, almost-smile<br><br>73 x laugh, laughed, laughing, laughs, laughter<br><br>25 x grin, grins, grinning<br><br><u>Makes a total of 221</u><br><br><br>30 x growls, growl, growly, growling<br><br>Rex had a tendency to growl a lot. <i>Um,</i> I shouldn't have been too surprised, should I?<br><br><br><br>The inner monologue is so tiresome.<br><br><i>Oh god, that is a classic blow-off. My face heats and my ears are ringing like they do whenever I'm fucking mortified. But I rip a corner off of the syllabus on my desk and lean over to write my cell number on it. Then I write Daniel, in case it's one of a dozen slips of paper with phone numbers Rex never intends to call. Christ, should I put my last name in case there's another Daniel?</i><br><br><br>More inner monologue for your perusal:<br><br><i>It's finally sinking in. I live here now. I live here in this tiny town. Everyone knows each other and I'm a stranger. They'll want to know me. Know about me. And then maybe they'll hate me.<br><br>(…)<br><br>Now, here I am. If I can just deal with my crappy apartment for one more year, I'll have enough money for a nicer place. If my car will just keep running for one more year, I'll be able to get a new one--well, a less-used one. Et cetera. One more year.</i><br><br><br><br><i>But beneath the stern expression is heat. It's dark and, okay, I can't see him that well, but I can feel his eyes drinking me in, sliding over my face and my body like he owns them. Me. Like there's not a force in the world that could stop him from taking whatever he wants from me. And I'll be damned if I wouldn't let him.</i><br><br><b>205 x okay</b><br><br>The word 'like' is also quite often used mid-sentence which I find annoying:<br><br><i>
  <b>Be friendly and, like, tell people things about yourself?<br><br>"I mean, this town only has, like, four restaurants."<br><br>Then I remember Ginger's admonition, realizing I've said, like, four words and half of them have been swear words.<br><br>He slides his chair back enough to pull me onto his lap, something I thought only happened to children and, like, cheerleaders or girls who were about to get proposed to.</b>
</i><br><br><br><i>I don't know what's wrong with me. I reach out a shaky hand to touch his back, then hesitate. Maybe he doesn't like being touched when we're not fucking?</i><br><br><br><i>"I don't know how to do this. What do I talk about? What if we actually hate each other?"</i><br><br>*cue eye roll*<br><br><i>"Um, Daniel. You don't hate each other. You had a date the other night and, even though you apparently refuse to tell me about it, it went well enough that you're having another one tomorrow. (…)"</i><br><br><br><u>Other <s>strange</s> annoying noises</u><br><br><i>Uuunnghhh<br>Uh<br>Ungh<br>Unnhh<br>Hunh<br>Mmphfhm<br>Hunh</i><br><br><br><u>Endearments</u><br>baby, sweetheart, sweetie, pumpkin and babycakes<br><br><br>I really dig the cover but otherwise nothing worked out for me. <i>
  <b>Um,</b>
</i> I wanted to give it less than two stars, but then readers would have accused me of being mean when I'm only being honest. I neither liked the corny writing style nor the characters in general and specifically the very <b>pesky</b> narrator, Daniel. So I come to the root of my misery. Daniel's constant 'ums' (if that should have been an "endearing" personality trait it backfired big time), his inner <s>monologue</s> ramblings and his issues in general killed this story for me. Daniel is highly needy, whiny and insecure and given the fact that he has a PhD in English, a prospective professor at that, his behavior astounded and infuriated me very much. I just could not for the life of me reconcile his personality issues and the way he talked with a <b>mature man in a teaching position.</b> Also, what irritated me tremendously was this…<br><br><b>
  <i>"Grading always infuriates me. It's like my students don't listen to what I say at all. I mean, we go over thesis statements in class and I give them a handout about how to tell if a thesis is strong or not. Then they write these papers and they're just nonsense. I mean, actual nonsense. (…)"</i>
</b><br><br>After reading that paragraph I was saying to myself: Daniel, you are a self-righteous and pretentious asshole. Not everyone is as "intelligent" (um, really…hunh…um…unnnhh…ungh…like...intelligent?) as you are. As a prospective professor, I expect much better from you. I believe you're in the wrong business. You'd better search for another vocation stat. *facepalm*<br><br>Rex said:<br><br><b>
  <i>"You don't know that," he says. "Maybe they're trying their best and they're just not as smart as you. Or they're good at math but not your class."</i>
</b><br><br>Daniel:<br><br><b>
  <i>Of course I know he's right. At every moment other than when I'm grading, I know that.<br>"You're right," I say. "I guess it just makes me feel like <u>I'm wasting my time trying to teach them shit</u> sometimes. Like they don't care about it anyway, so why do I spend all my time trying to make them?"<br><br>(…)<br><br>Rex doesn't say anything. His shoulders are tense and his jaw clenched. He must think I'm such a pretentious ass right now. Really, it's never a good idea to grade while anyone else is watching.</i>
</b><br><br>Yep, you better shut your trap, <s>Dan</s> Dick. He made generalizations, was quick to judge and, even worse, lumped them together. I suppose that Daniel should have been portrayed as the poor sod with the puppy dog eyes, yet I just could not sympathize with this annoying prick.<br><br>On another note, I found it very interesting that Daniel who'd been a top, was ready to bottom immediately. <i>Um</i>…you know, he couldn't wait to let Rex stick his dick in his hole. I mean, <i>
  <b>like,</b>
</i> rather sooner than later.<br><br>Another issue I had was Daniel pushing the <s>alleged tear gland</s> repetitiveness button by saying <i>'No one has ever done this for me, no one has touched me like this, or cared for me like this'</i> one too many times. Repetitiveness is one of my biggest pet peeves and as you can gather it got on my last nerve. <br><br><i>
  <b>"Do you want me to take care of you? Make sure you're relaxed?" Is that a trick question? Do I want him to take care of me? What does that mean? I don't want Rex to think I'm weak, but I don't want him to stop. I want this to be like a dream, where things just happen and one talks about them and everything is liquid and sleepy. I wish I were drunk so I could let him do whatever he wants to me and it wouldn't have to be my choice. I don't think I'm supposed to wish for that.</b>
</i><br><br>Sticking to the common and trite repetitiveness, it goes without saying that we have lots of body appreciation once again. Rex is huge, <b>
  <i>like,</i>
</b> bodybuilder-huge. <i>Um,</i> I got that too. There's no need to beat a dead horse. <i>Um…okay?</i><br><br>Around the 37% mark, there was an argument which escalated quickly and instead of addressing the problem and asking a simple question, Daniel lapsed into his common inner idiocy and acted like an immature kid and not like a thirty-year-old teacher. Whatever.<br><br>I have enjoyed, even devoured, quiet story lines in the past. This being said, it's very unfortunate that In the Middle of Somewhere fell totally flat in that regard. To be very straightforward, it was a total bore because it lacked tension and irresistibility. Nothing really appealed to me. During the prologue, when Rex helped Daniel out in the woods, brought him to his cottage and, after a kiss, slept in the same bed, they left me kind of perplexed. I didn't feel their chemistry. Later, when Daniel got the teaching position and came back to Michigan, a lot of things and/or situations were too awkward for me. But, as you can see, I'm only one of a few readers who didn't enjoy it. So it might as well be me and not the book. I think, however, that if the author could tone down the sugar factor and endow her characters with other traits, make them more likable, that is, I would actually enjoy her writing. <br><br>As it was, In the Middle of Somewhere proved to be another bust. Movin' on...<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423755386ra/13667481.gif" alt=" photo oie_GTO7bs0C5cnv_zpsct2xyhna.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1303488401" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1303488401" />
    <a title="Gigi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11550843-gigi"><img alt="Gigi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538251705p2/11550843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1303488401?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gigi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gigi" href="/user/show/11550843-gigi">Gigi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25862832-in-the-middle-of-somewhere">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11550843-gigi?shelf=mm-contemporary">mm-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11550843-gigi?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11550843-gigi?shelf=gay-book-reviews">gay-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11550843-gigi?shelf=mm-healing-comfort">mm-healing-comfort</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11550843-gigi?shelf=fuck-yeah-5-plus-stars">fuck-yeah-5-plus-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11550843-gigi?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11550843-gigi?shelf=mm-pure-romance">mm-pure-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1303488401" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14092646071155816248"><b>Roan Parrish is nominated for Best Debut Author at Goodreads for In the Middle of Somewhere! Vote vote vote! It is SUCH a fabulous book! <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/choiceawards/best-debut-goodreads-author-2015'>https://www.goodreads.com/choiceaward...</a></b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435887922i/15384999.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>WARNING: This review will contain some <i>serious</i> fangirling.</b><br/><br/>This book is by first time author <a href='http://roanparrish.com/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Roan Parrish</a>, but after reading this, you probably won't believe that. You might think, oh, Roan is just a pseudonym for <a href='http://nrwalker.wordpress.com/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>N.R. Walker</a> or <a href='http://www.greenshill.com/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amy Lane</a> or <a href='http://www.kamitchell.com/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>K.A. Mitchell</a> or any of the talented authors who write fabulous warm 'n fuzzy, ang</span>
  <span id="freeText14092646071155816248" style="display:none"><b>Roan Parrish is nominated for Best Debut Author at Goodreads for In the Middle of Somewhere! Vote vote vote! It is SUCH a fabulous book! <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/choiceawards/best-debut-goodreads-author-2015">https://www.goodreads.com/choiceaward...</a></b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435887922i/15384999.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>WARNING: This review will contain some <i>serious</i> fangirling.</b><br><br>This book is by first time author <a href="http://roanparrish.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Roan Parrish</a>, but after reading this, you probably won't believe that. You might think, oh, Roan is just a pseudonym for <a href="http://nrwalker.wordpress.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">N.R. Walker</a> or <a href="http://www.greenshill.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy Lane</a> or <a href="http://www.kamitchell.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">K.A. Mitchell</a> or any of the talented authors who write fabulous warm 'n fuzzy, angsty, contemporary M/M romances. Because this book isn't just good. It's <i>that</i> good. 	<br><br>Daniel Mulligan is a bright and talented college graduate working on his dissertation. He needs a teaching job to get his feet wet in the academic community and make some money to pay off his enormous student loan debt. The pickings are slim and the only college who offers him a job is in a small town in Michigan. Daniel was born and bred in Philadelphia, so he is in real culture shock living in a tiny community where everyone knows everyone's business. When he interviewed for the job six months ago, he made the acquaintance of a very large, gentle soul named Rex Vale. During this meeting, Rex shelters Daniel in his cabin after a minor fender-bender, sets and bandages a dog's leg that was hit by Daniel's car, cooks him real, honest to goodness food, provides him with clothes too large for him and a nice, a hot shower and a peaceful night on the couch watching movies and drinking whiskey. One thing leads to another and Daniel ends up kissing Rex in a drunken moment of venerability. While Rex does kiss him back, he refuses any other advances and puts Daniel in bed for the night. When Daniel wakes up, Rex is gone but leaves him coffee, toast and the number for a cab company for a ride to the airport.<br><br>Six months later, Daniel is back and getting settled into his new home (a pretty shitty apartment with a <i>very</i> uncomfortable bed) before he begins work at the local college as an English Professor. He has not been able to get the strong, silent Rex out of his mind during that six months and hopes to see him again. Soon.<br><br>Low and behold, Rex and Daniel do cross paths again when Daniel is out for a walk and Rex's dog (the one hit by Daniel's car) jumps on him and knocks him down. The passion that has been simmering in Daniel for six months comes to a head and the men end up getting each other off next to a tree.<br><br>It is slow going and weeks pass between seeing each other, but eventually these men start a relationship. The sex is <i>great</i>, the company pleasant and Rex helps Daniel with his homesickness for Philly.<br><br>We get to see the full progression of Daniel and Rex's relationship and the hurdles they need to jump through to make it work. There are a few bumps in the road, mainly relating to each others family, but nothing they can't overcome together. The angst level is quite low for the most part. Also, this book is told entirely from Daniel's POV, so we get a lot more out of Daniel's character than Rex's. But it is an undisputed fact that these guys are <i>crazy</i> about each other.<br><br>OK, I am not even kidding a little bit. I honestly want to make a 6 stars shelf because I think this book might be <i>too</i> good for the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/11550843-gigi?shelf=fuck-yeah-5-plus-stars&amp;utf8=%E2%9C%93" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Fuck Yeah, 5+ Stars</a> shelf. The way these boys handle their feelings for one another, the way they are both good, honest people (not a mean bone in their bodies) and the love that comes through the pages is a <b>masterpiece</b>. I can guarantee you that you will fall head-over-heals for Rex and want him to be your pretend book boyfriend. And the epilogue is wonderful and leaves you thinking and <i>knowing</i> that these boys have reached their HEA.	<br><br>I can <b>HIGHLY, HIGHLY, HIGHLY recommend</b> this book to just about <i>everyone</i>. The only people I can think of that won't like this one are folks who like the dark side of their M/M stories at the exclusion of all others. <br><br><a href="http://roanparrish.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Roan Parrish</a> reminds me of other, newer authors who came out of the gate at full speed like <a href="http://renaekaye.weebly.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Renae Kaye</a>, <a href="http://www.rileyhartwrites.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Riley Hart</a>, <a href="http://www.letablake.wordpress.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Leta Blake</a>, <a href="http://www.riverjaymes.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">River Jaymes</a>. <br><br>I cannot <b>WAIT</b> to read her next book.<br><br><i>Shit, that was some serious fangirl vomit, huh?</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435887922i/15385000.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> This review is also posted at <a href="http://gaybook.reviews/2015/07/02/in-the-middle-of-somewhere/" rel="nofollow noopener">Gay Book Reviews</a><br><br><a href="http://gaybook.reviews/2015/07/02/in-the-middle-of-somewhere/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446675884i/16864288.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>	 </span>
  <a data-text-id="14092646071155816248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1303280236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3892366670782874685"><b>WARNING #1:</b> This review is brought to you by Grumpy Kat™ and contains <i>"unpopular opinions."</i> <br/><br/><b>WARNING #2:</b> If you are one of those people who have an issue with negative reviews that contain quotes to get a point across because you feel they are unfair and taken out of context, then MOVE. ALONG. There's nothing for you to see here. <br/><br/>I apologise in advance for how long and rambling and lacking in eloquence this review is. <br/><br/>Right. To say I was looking forward to reading this would be a massive understa</span>
  <span id="freeText3892366670782874685" style="display:none"><b>WARNING #1:</b> This review is brought to you by Grumpy Kat™ and contains <i>"unpopular opinions."</i> <br /><br /><b>WARNING #2:</b> If you are one of those people who have an issue with negative reviews that contain quotes to get a point across because you feel they are unfair and taken out of context, then MOVE. ALONG. There's nothing for you to see here. <br /><br />I apologise in advance for how long and rambling and lacking in eloquence this review is. <br /><br />Right. To say I was looking forward to reading this would be a massive understatement. It was definitely a clear-the-decks-so-I-can-read-it-immediately-upon-release kind of book. So to be as disappointed and underwhelmed by it as I am, well, it makes my heart hurt a little bit. <br /><br />Without further ado, let's get to the reasons why Grumpy Kat™ was activated. <br /><br />1. The pacing. <br />A few weeks back, I read a really beautiful excerpt from this. It was a short scene that had the two MCs, Daniel &amp; Rex, sharing a kiss. Even though it wasn't defined, it gave off the impression that this was their first kiss. I cannot stress to you how lovely I thought this was and it made me so excited to read the book properly because any build up leading to a first kiss as lovely as that, had to be good, right? WRONG. The problem was, this kiss (which, incidentally, was their first one) happened at only 5% into the book and came after they hadn't known each other for very long. Don't get me wrong, I can enjoy insta-whatever, but it doesn't work for me if the couple doesn't have enough time to establish some chemistry. So considering how Daniel &amp; Rex met? I just wasn't buying what went on here. A consequence to missing the mark like this means it can leave the rest of the story unbalanced and lacking tension. Furthermore, there's going to be problems with the pacing if the relationship itself is low angst and the book is this long and meandering. <br />Creating conflict over the breaking of a table is a fail. <br />Revealing at 40% the MC has suffered a trauma in his past and then resolving the fall out from that by 45% is a fail. <br />Saving the main source of conflict until after 70% with it possibly being done as a way to set up a forthcoming book is a fail. <br /><br />2. The narrator. <br />I have yet to read a book where I have actively disliked the narrator but still managed to love the book. <br />Strike one: Daniel was a 30 year old man but at times he read like an 18 year old YA/NA protagonist trapped inside the body of a 30 year old. Which was just. . . no. It was really brought home how much younger he appeared when he was on page with a character named Leo who <i>was</i> 18, because the way they both talked (not including Leo's propensity for talking with unnecessary exclamation marks!) was indistinguishable from one another. <br />Strike two: Daniel's inner monologues were terminally boring. I honestly gave no fucks about what he was thinking - especially when it was about teaching crap, or how big Rex's hands were, or how he wasn't worthy of good things.<br />Strike three: Daniel was an über whiny Judgy McJudgypants. He was a slightly judgemental dick while at the same time lamenting people who might judge him for being gay and covered in tattoos. Seriously? What the fuck is up with that? If the purpose of making him be that way was to elicit sympathy for his hard knock life, then I've got to be honest and say it didn't work. <br />An example of said boring monologue which manages to include some of my gripes about him in just the one paragraph: <blockquote>
  <i>What the fuck is wrong with me? Unlike my inability to answer Rex, I can think of about a hundred answers to that question. Like, I barely know this guy, so why am I so goddamned worried about what he thinks of me? Like, I should’ve left last night after we fucked and I don’t get why I didn’t. Like, I’ve never had a real relationship, so why would I start now?</i>
</blockquote> And here's a quote from one of Daniel's less boring inner monologues that sums up what I feel about him perfectly: <blockquote>
  <i>I'd know his name and who was in his daily life, but I'd be waiting to find out that thing that would make me care about his story.</i>
</blockquote> I had the misfortune of being in his head for way more than 300 pages and there wasn't anything I read in all that time that made me care even once. <br /><br /><br />Now we get to the semi-ranty portion of the review. <br /><br />3. Repetition, repetition, repetition, repetition, REPI-FUCKING-TITION. <br />The one thing I absolutely detest above all else when I read is repetition. It's distracting, I'm never able to look past it and unfortunately for books/authors, I'm like a heat-seeking missile when it comes to spotting it. <i>In the Middle of Somewhere</i> was incredibly guilty of repetition. <br /><br />For your reading pleasure, I have the roll of <s>dis</s>honour of repetitve shit Part #1: <br /><br /><b>Um:</b> <blockquote>
  <i>His hand is huge. "I, <b>um,</b>" He bends down and looks in my face. <br /><br />"What the hell? "<b>Um,</b>" I say. <br /><br />He slides my suit jacket off my shoulders and starts to unbutton my shirt. "<b>Um,</b>" I mumble. <br /><br />"Take your pants off." "Oh, <b>um,</b> I—" <br /><br />"Why Marilyn?" "Like Marilyn Monroe—she just, <b>um,</b>—you know, she was a little banged up, so I figured she could use a star's name.<br /><br />"Changing the subject: check. <b>Um,</b> he's.... Well, he's...." <br /><br />"I'll have to see. I'm here for this year at least. <b>Um....</b>" <br /><br />He still doesn't want my number, or....? "<b>Um,</b> yeah, I'll see you," I say. <br /><br />I take her large paw in my hand and shake it. "<b>Um.</b> Good night."</i>
</blockquote> Um, repeat, um, ad, um, nauseum. <br /><br /><b>Oh:</b> <blockquote>
  <i>"<b>Oh,</b>" I say. <br /><br />"<b>Oh,</b> yeah." <br /><br />"<b>Oh,</b> I'm Daniel." <br /><br />"<b>Oh,</b> so that'll take you, what, two or three years?" <br /><br />"<b>Oh,</b> it's boring; you don't want to hear about that," <br /><br />"What? <b>Oh."</b> I laugh, looking at the dog. <br /><br />He's looking at the dog, not me. "<b>Oh,</b> yeah, thanks." I look down too. "<b>Oh</b> shit." <br /><br />"<b>Oh, oh,</b>" I cry out. <br /><br />"That's pretty grim," he says. "<b>Oh,</b> don't worry about it. I'm doing laundry tomorrow.</i>
</blockquote> Oh, and repeat ad nauseum. <br /><br /><b>I mean:</b> <blockquote>
  <i>It isn't something I'm used to—quiet, <b>I mean. </b><br /><br />"You were in an accident?" "Are you hurt?" "No—<b>I mean,</b> I'm not." <br /><br />"You're a film geek, huh?" "What? No. <b>I mean,</b> I just like old movies," <br /><br />"I can't stop thinking about him, Ginge. It's idiotic. <b>I mean,</b> I barely know the guy." <br /><br />I don't pine. I don't wonder what they're doing. I never have. <b>I mean,</b> sure, I've had crushes. <br /><br />"I didn't know you were going to keep her. I hope—<b>I mean,</b> I hope you didn't feel obligated or anything," <br /><br />"We get along pretty good. Well, <b>I mean.</b> We get along very well." <br /><br /><b>I mean,</b> it was so cool of you to let me stay and then I just kind of jumped on you and—anyway.<br /><br />"Just stay left. I can drive you if you want. <b>I mean,</b> I need to go back home and get my truck, but—"</i>
</blockquote> I mean, repeat ad nauseum. <br /><br /><b>Smell/smells/smelled:</b> <blockquote>
  <i>[...] but I crack the window to breathe the sweet <b>smell</b> of fresh air and trees anyway. <br /><br />The fire consumes the paper and there's a delicious, earthy <b>smell</b> as the bark on the logs starts to crackle. <br /><br />He's looking at me calmly and I can <b>smell</b> him on the blanket I'm wrapped in. <br /><br />God, it's such a familiar <b>smell.</b> <br /><br />The fire is crackling and the <b>smell</b> of wood smoke combined with Rex's scent is heady. <br /><br />It <b>smells</b> heavenly. <br /><br />As if in sympathy, the ghost <b>smells</b> of oil, lube and hot metal tickle my sinuses. <br /><br />"He was skinny and <b>smelled</b> like cloves and he said he liked Kurt Vile." <br /><br />But he's warm, even in a T-shirt, and he <b>smells</b> so good.</i>
</blockquote> Make sure you have a good smell before you repeat ad nauseum. <br /><br /><b>Smile/smiles/smiled:</b> <blockquote>
  <i> He hasn't <b>smiled</b> yet, but he probably has a nice one. <br /><br />"Better?" he asks, and when he gives me his first real <b>smile,</b> it's the sweetest thing I've ever seen. <br /><br />I murmur. He <b>smiles</b> at me. <br /><br />Rex quirks an eyebrow. "Only with you," I say. His <b>smile</b> is slow and predatory. <br /><br />I'm joking but he doesn't <b>smile.</b> <br /><br />She <b>smiles</b> broadly at me, but her <b>smile</b> fades when she looks down to my arms. <br /><br />Jesus, Daniel. Rex laughs, his <b>smile</b> wide. <br /><br />Rex grins and it almost takes my breath away. It's a <b>smile</b> that reaches all the way to his whiskey-coloured eyes, wrinkling at the corners.<br /><br />"Don't argue; just accept it," Marjorie says, and I <b>smile.</b></i>
</blockquote> *smiles winningly* Repeat ad nauseum. <br /><br /><b>Like:</b> <blockquote>
  <i> I keep seeing, <b>like,</b> cherries in all the salads here. <br /><br />"Maybe I'll keep the shop open and only give Thanksgiving-themed tattoos. But, <b>like,</b> literal ones. <b>Like,</b> I'll tattoo turkeys, Thanksgiving foods, the genocide of indigenous peoples, et cetera. Whattaya think? <br /><br />"Um, no offense or anything," he says, "and I'm sure it's a good album and all, but that's kind of a lame present for someone who, <b>like,</b> carved you something out of a tree with his bare hands." <br /><br />"Yeah, <b>like,</b> what nice things, so I don't repeat them." <br /><br />"<b>Like,</b> because I know we haven't had that conversation, I know." <br /><br /><b>Like,</b> what's so special about the things we hide away anyway? <br /><br />"At school, people thought I was... <b>like,</b> learning disabled because I never talked and I..." <br /><br />"<b>Like,</b> you know that feeling." <br /><br />So, I drop the bagel and I'm just <b>like</b> swearing a blue streak, right? <br /><br />And he looks at glasses guy behind the counter in horror—<b>like,</b> what the hell did you do to make this lady lose her shit.</i>
</blockquote> Like, repeat ad nauseum, like. <br /><br />I think it's worth noting that a lot of this wasn't just said by Daniel. If it was, I could <i>maybe</i> put it down to being a quirk of his and part of his vernacular, but as it happened with ALL of the characters, I was left in a state of being perma-growly. <br /><br />4. The sex. <br />My lovely buddy reader also had a problem with this—but her issue was she felt there was too much. I, on the other hand, didn't have an issue with how much there was, I had ISSUES with what was said, described and what went on. <br /><br />The roll of <s>dis</s>honour of repetitve shit Part #2—The Sex Edition: <br /><br /><b>Channel:</b> <blockquote>
  <i>"Oh fuck," he says, but it's like his voice is coming from a great distance, far away from the feeling of his fingers zinging pleasure through my <b>channel</b> and his big hand stroking us together faster now. <br /><br />And then, in the space of a heartbeat, we're one body, melted together as my <b>channel</b> adjusts to his size and he relaxes into me. <br /><br />Every time he fills me he brushes over the spot that makes my whole <b>channel</b> pulse with pleasure. <br /><br />The only thing I can feel is the empty throbbing in my <b>channel</b> where his tongue left me wanting. <br /><br />It's like his whole <b>channel</b> is a fist, squeezing me. <br /><br />I can feel my whole <b>channel</b> throbbing with pleasure and a little bit of soreness from his powerful thrusts.</i>
</blockquote> <b>Pulse/pulses/pulsing:</b> <blockquote>
  <i> Every scrape of his teeth sends a <b>pulse</b> to my groin. <br /><br />His cock is so hard he's <b>pulsing</b> against me and I can tell it took some effort to even form the words.<br /><br />I can feel his erection <b>pulse</b> against my ass with the beat of his heart. <br /><br />My own cock gives a final, sympathetic <b>pulse,</b> a few last beads of pleasure welling from me as Rex collapses on my back, his breath loud in my ear.</i>
</blockquote> (As an aside, Kat Fact #171: My favourite kind of pulse is a sympathetic one. True story.) <blockquote>
  <i>I cry out at his words, my eyes squeezing shut as he <b>pulses</b> his finger against my prostate and my whole channel throbs with pleasure.</i>
</blockquote> Yeeeeeah. So lots of pulsing and channel bidness went on... But that wasn't all. When it came to sex, poor Rex wasn't portrayed in the best light. <br /><br />The man has a thick arse. <br /><br />And a fluttering hole. <br /><br />And he produces his own scent - Eau de Arousal.<br /><br />And when his mouth was in the vicinity of Daniel's nipples it was shivery. <br /><br />And his dong tastes <i>salty and a little sweet, like a hot martini.</i> ! ! ! ! ! !<br /><br />Annnnd he also suffered with a weeping erection which, when I read it, resulted in this conversation with my buddy reader: <br /><br />Me: Rex has a weeping erection. Does it mean it's crying? <br />Her: It's sad for the writing. <br />Me: What has an erection got to be sad about? <br />Her: It's featured as an extension of big, strong Rex. And his big hands. <br />Me: Do you think it's sad about all the pulsing? <br /><i>"I pump him firmly and his hips pulse, driving me even deeper inside him. I can barely think. Every beat of my heart is thumping in my ears, pulsing in my stomach, and pushing blood into my cock until I feel like one big heartbeat, pulsing inside Rex's body."</i> <br />Her: She missed out that Rex's body is big. <br />Me: Maybe that's why the erection started weeping. If the erection 'ums' then this will be a dnf. <br />Her: If there's a talking erection, it's a whole different book. <br />Me: I would read that book. <br /><br />Moving on! <br /><br />There was also inconsistencies and moments of what the fuckery? during some of the sex scenes that caused my buddy reader to dub me a Sex CSI after I began dissecting the minutiae of them. Pay attention, class, so I can explain what I mean. <blockquote>
  <i>He kneels between my legs, spreading them to make room for him, and kneads my inner thighs and up to the crease of my bottom. He takes me by the hips and digs strong thumbs into my spine, pushing my knees up and apart.</i>
</blockquote> There isn't actually anything wrong with what is described here. After all, Daniel is laying on his stomach and Rex is between his legs doing his thing before moving his legs into what would be a kneeling position if his knees were pushed up and apart, right? But then if you continue to read the rest of the paragraph, you get this: <blockquote>
  <i>I squirm a little, trying to maneuver myself into a position that isn’t crushing my burgeoning erection.</i>
</blockquote> After reading that is when I became confused. He was seemingly manoeuvred into a kneeling position, but if he was, then how could his erection be getting crushed? Does he have a dong that is comparable in size to a T-Rex's? Unlikely. So none of that made sense. <br /><br />Then there was also this from the very next paragraph: <blockquote>
  <i>Rex lifts my hips easily and settles me back on the bed tenderly, then urges me down again, his attention returning to my ass.</i>
</blockquote> Hmmm. His hips were lifted which proves he wasn't kneeling before, so how on earth were his knees pushed up and apart if he was laying on his stomach? Once again things don't make sense. Now if we take that last quote and analyse it on its own, you'll see it's also illogical because Daniel is lifted up by his hips and then settled back down, so if he is already on the bed, then how is it possible for him to be urged down again? <br /><br />Gah! So many questions!<br /><br />A good sex scene allows you, the reader, to be swept up in the moment. A good sex scene wouldn't allow you to get distracted by incorrect or implausible details because someone should have picked up on them in the first place. <br /><br /><br />Essentially, why I think this didn't work for me was because it was just too much. Too much of the stuff that doesn't matter or belong there - which was to the detriment of the stuff that should. Also, I should point out that I do know the problems I had with the pacing and MC are purely subjective, but the repetition and inconsistencies during the sex scenes are not and nor should they be. Those problems are ones that shouldn't even be there and any excuses made to the contrary are only doing a disservice to readers who are entitled to get the best book they possibly can. <br /><br />And finally. If anyone thinks about coming on to my review space to tell me I'm wrong because a lot of other people love this book, or that I should be kind and cut the author some slack because she's a newbie, then prepare to feel my wrath before I block you. I know I'm very much in the minority with my thoughts, but all of this is just <i>my</i> opinion, okay?</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1313360246" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6670803027965764671"><b>~3.5~</b><br/><br/><b>This is a strong debut with sharp writing and well sketched characters.</b> <br/><br/>Because the book is told from Daniel's POV, we are aware of his ramblings and insecurities. <br/><br/>But what about Rex, the shy, withdrawn carpenter? <br/><br/>I adored Rex. Rex is the boyfriend everyone wants: sculpted like a god, kind, smart, an awesome listener, good with animals, and really, REALLY good with his hands. <br/><br/>I desperately wanted Rex's POV; being in Daniel's head that long was a little annoying. <br/><br/>Daniel and Rex's relationshi</span>
  <span id="freeText6670803027965764671" style="display:none"><b>~3.5~</b><br /><br /><b>This is a strong debut with sharp writing and well sketched characters.</b> <br /><br />Because the book is told from Daniel's POV, we are aware of his ramblings and insecurities. <br /><br />But what about Rex, the shy, withdrawn carpenter? <br /><br />I adored Rex. Rex is the boyfriend everyone wants: sculpted like a god, kind, smart, an awesome listener, good with animals, and really, REALLY good with his hands. <br /><br />I desperately wanted Rex's POV; being in Daniel's head that long was a little annoying. <br /><br />Daniel and Rex's relationship may be a case of insta-lust, but it's certainly not insta-love. Not counting the first chapter, the book spans five months and more than 6,000 locations. <br /><br /><b>I'm going to say it: this book felt LONG, too long. </b><br /><br />Don't get me wrong; I usually enjoy long novels. But some of Daniel's inner monologue felt redundant, and the story didn't grab me right away.<br /><br />I loved the heat between Daniel and Rex, but I wanted them to get to it already (and I don't mean sex ... just general togetherness). <br /><br />The sex scenes, however, were pitch perfect, so fucking steamy I could barely breathe. <b>Huge A+++ for the HAWT, raw SEX. The guys start off fucking against a tree and go from there. <br /><br />MAJOR SMEX APPEAL!</b><br /><br />I liked the focus on the relationship, although I didn't love all the secondary characters. And Daniel's family? What a bunch of douchebags. <br /><br />The epilogue was a little disappointing too, although the ending is a HEA. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I just wanted Daniel and Rex, not Daniel and Ginger. I had enough of Ginger in general.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />To summarize: great chemistry, serious sexy action, interesting MCs, awesome dog named Marilyn, strong writing, BUT needed a dual POV and too wordy with sections that dragged (for me). <br /><br />P.S. Rounded UP for Rex alone. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6670803027965764671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3068938-mirjana-dtr---down-to-read?shelf=cry-me-a-river">cry-me-a-river</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1315826676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2308061923950287980"><br/><b>**1/12/17 - Re-read via Audiobook. I need some Rex in my life right now. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451914065ra/17620622.gif' height='209' width='500' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>1/26/17 - Finished my audiobook reread and though I'm leaving my rating below the same, I've decided to round up to 5 stars. I loved this book EVEN MORE the second time around and it just doesn't feel right rounding it down to a 4 star. I still stand behind my thoughts that some of Daniel's ramblings could have been edited out, but damn....this book is so damn wonderful! </b><br/><br/>-----------------------------------------------<br/><br/><b>***4.5</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2308061923950287980" style="display:none"><br><b>**1/12/17 - Re-read via Audiobook. I need some Rex in my life right now. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451914065ra/17620622.gif" height="209" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>1/26/17 - Finished my audiobook reread and though I'm leaving my rating below the same, I've decided to round up to 5 stars. I loved this book EVEN MORE the second time around and it just doesn't feel right rounding it down to a 4 star. I still stand behind my thoughts that some of Daniel's ramblings could have been edited out, but damn....this book is so damn wonderful! </b><br><br>-----------------------------------------------<br><br><b>***4.5 Stars***</b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"As long as I'm with you, I'll be home."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I absolutely ADORED and LOVED Rex and Daniel and their love story!! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434003236ra/15167186.gif" alt="description" height="450" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That's exactly what this book is....a true love story....and a beautifully quiet one at that. Not too much angst, no crazy, over the top drama...just a beautiful story about two men scarred by their childhood looking for a human connection, unconditional love and a sense of home. <br><br>Daniel is the youngest of four boys. Completely different than his macho mechanic brothers. He's an academic, not very interested in cars...and gay. His father and brothers have no idea how to relate to him so they alienate him. They make fun of his sexual orientation and think he's snooty and a know-it-all for pursuing a graduate degree.<br><br>He finds himself in a a nowhere town in Michigan student teaching. One fateful night he runs into Rex and their connection is instantaneous. Is it insta-lust? Hell yes. These two are completely combustible and scorching hot!! Is it insta-love? Not at all. <br><br>Michigan is so different from Daniel's life in Philadelphia. He doesn't have his usual outlets to hide behind. No bars, no booze, no random hookups...not even his best friend (and only friend) Ginger. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>There's nowhere to hide here. No blending in or fucking off. I've never felt so terrified or so exposed.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Rex is a bear of a man. Tall, strong and burly...but sweet, compassionate and tender down to his bones. Rex lives in a cabin in the woods. He's kind of the town maintenance man. He does odd jobs for people who need it, but he spends most of his time in his woodshop making furniture. He keeps his head down and doesn't interact with people much. He's shy and a bit of a recluse. Due to his nomadic childhood and other issues, he has a hard time connecting and opening up to others. But there's something about Daniel...the two share a connection that can't be denied. A comfort with each other that flows easily. <br><br>Daniel's never met anyone quite like Rex. It unnerves him how quickly he's become comfortable with Rex. He's terrified of what it all means, but completely mesmerized by the sensations Rex pulls out of him. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>No one has ever touched me like this. Cared for me like this. It's like Rex thinks of my body as something he's responsible for. Something precious.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>He touches me all the time. It's almost like he doesn't notice it. Like I'm just an extension of his body and so of course he would touch me. But, no, that makes it sound thoughtless. It's like when I'm near him he decides that it's his right to touch me. It makes me feel so connected to him.</blockquote>

</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430199226ra/14691569.gif" height="295" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Their romance is a slow burn. Almost a living breathing thing slowly growing, evolving, adapting and fusing two lonely hearts.<br><br>Told entirely from Daniel's POV, you really see him struggle to accept that good things can happen to him...that someone like Rex could love and care for him. But you also feel Rex's emotions. His shy vulnerability peeks through with quiet actions, soft touches and whispered words. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"I think you're perfect. I mean, shit, that sounded sappy, but, I mean perfect in my opinion." Ugh, how do I explain what I mean? That all those things that he is came together like the perfect recipe.<br><br>"For you?" Rex says.<br><br>"Hmm?"<br><br>"Perfect for you, maybe?" He looks shy and pleased. All I can do is nod.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Little by little both men begin to realize that what they have is real and deep and important...and meaningful. They easily open up to each other about their pasts, their childhoods, their fears and their dreams. Shy and vulnerable Rex begins to put scarred and broken Daniel back together again. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>There's something about Rex that makes me feel calm. As if I'm scattered until the moment I see him and when he touches me I fly back together in a configuration that makes sense. </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>And Daniel gives Rex the outlet he needs to be the man he wants to be. To care for someone, to put roots down with someone and to build a life with someone. To have someone accept him wholeheartedly and unconditionally. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Maybe the point of I LOVE YOU is that it IS a tether. A connection so you can find your way back to someone even when shit seems huge and unmanageable on your own. A promise to help just because you care about someone, a promise to help that doesn't mean pulling away.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Both men grow and become better versions of themselves with the love of the other (even though Rex was pretty perfect already in my eyes). They complete each other, help each other and ultimately, unconditionally love each other. <br><br>They've found the stability and home they were both looking for and were pleasantly surprised to find that it wasn't in a small town in Michigan or in a cabin in the woods....it was with each other. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"The other night, you said that we mean different things when we say I love you. That you don't know what it means to have someone love you. This is what it means. It means doing things together and learning what each other needs. I give you what you need. You give me what I need. And they're not the same. And that's fine. It's not too good to be true. It's just good."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405929ra/791415.gif" height="282" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Rex and Daniel absolutely stole my heart. My heart was beating out of my chest at the beauty, sensuality, passion and love pouring out of every touch and tender moment. Was it hard being only in Daniel's head at times? Yes. Would I have liked a little bit from Rex's POV? Yes. But I understood that this was a deeper journey for Daniel. He had more to accept, more to overcome, more to feel. And just because you don't get Rex's POV, doesn't mean you don't feel every bit of him as well. <br><br>So all this gushing and why not 5 stars? I feel like the book is too long and could have been edited down. There was too much rambling and too many tangents that didn't add anything to the story or character development. This book could EASILY be trimmed down and you would get the exact same emotion. <br><br>For a debut novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14070842.Roan_Parrish" title="Roan Parrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Roan Parrish</a> made quite the entrance in my opinion. With a beautiful story of two lonely men looking for home, she's made a huge fan in me. I can't wait to see what else is in store from her!<br><br><br>------------------------------------------<br><br><b>Between the blurb and THAT cover....</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380743475ra/3118206.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2308061923950287980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1770013631?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dia" href="/user/show/27899735-dia">Dia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781634762120" href="/book/show/25687508-in-the-middle-of-somewhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27899735-dia?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27899735-dia?shelf=my-first-by-this-author">my-first-by-this-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27899735-dia?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27899735-dia?shelf=best-2017">best-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27899735-dia?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27899735-dia?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27899735-dia?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27899735-dia?shelf=the-best">the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27899735-dia?shelf=hot-hot-hot">hot-hot-hot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27899735-dia?shelf=300-400-pages">300-400-pages</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1770013631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10187639837959917705"><b>All the stars</b><br/><br/>I can't believe how much <b>I adored this book!</b> I've read it in one sitting. <br/>This author surely knows how to develop the action. I got super invested into the story. So much that I just couldn't seem to put it down. I was dying to read more. Now I keep wondering what took me so long to get to it! <br/><br/>I loved the writing, the story, the MC's and yes, I simply adored Rex!!! He was so kind and sweet even if he was a mountain of a man. <br/><br/>I just can't believe <b>this is the author's debut book!</b> I bo</span>
  <span id="freeText10187639837959917705" style="display:none"><b>All the stars</b><br /><br />I can't believe how much <b>I adored this book!</b> I've read it in one sitting. <br />This author surely knows how to develop the action. I got super invested into the story. So much that I just couldn't seem to put it down. I was dying to read more. Now I keep wondering what took me so long to get to it! <br /><br />I loved the writing, the story, the MC's and yes, I simply adored Rex!!! He was so kind and sweet even if he was a mountain of a man. <br /><br />I just can't believe <b>this is the author's debut book!</b> I bow my head before her! I really couldn't stop reading. Rex and Daniel were super HOT together. I love how their relationship developed and the ending was extremely sweet. I hope we'll get a chance to revisit them in book #2. <br /><br />There were some surprises on the road and I was extremely happy with the secondary characters: <b>Leo and Ginger.</b> I think I adored this story more because of them. Ohhh, they were the cherries on the cake for me. <br />I just LOVE to chuckle while reading. I think this gives a good book what it takes to become a great one. At least for me. It's not easy for a writer to give his characters good humor. I think here Roan Parrish did a great job by creating these secondary characters who gave me such great vibes and well added uniqueness to the story. Rainbows and unicorns are easy to develop. Great humor, not really.<br /><br /><b>I adored sassy Leo.</b> He really is a younger version of Daniel and I completely get why they became friends. I saw we get his story in book #3. And I can't believe his love interest is no one else than Will!!! Oh I simply adore his smart mouth! He also seems to have a strong personality. I wonder what he hides. <br /><br />I can't wait to read more from this author.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10187639837959917705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1326104458?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24626621-catherine?shelf=super-sweet-studs">super-sweet-studs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24626621-catherine?shelf=blue-collar-babes">blue-collar-babes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24626621-catherine?shelf=nerd-love">nerd-love</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1326104458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18343944061970509797">Fantastic debut novel from Roan Parrish!<br/><br/>What I loved:<br/><br/>* Rex - I loved EVERYTHING about that man! He may have been a tad <i>too</i> perfect (read: unrealistically so), but you won't hear me complaining. Every time I thought he'd shown us the best of him, Roan peeled back another layer and I was toast. <br/><br/>* the super steamy sex. These guys had great chemistry together and HOLY GOD was Rex <b>thorough</b> in the bedroom! ...and in the shower ...and against (multiple) trees. If you read this book and say that you don</span>
  <span id="freeText18343944061970509797" style="display:none">Fantastic debut novel from Roan Parrish!<br /><br />What I loved:<br /><br />* Rex - I loved EVERYTHING about that man! He may have been a tad <i>too</i> perfect (read: unrealistically so), but you won't hear me complaining. Every time I thought he'd shown us the best of him, Roan peeled back another layer and I was toast. <br /><br />* the super steamy sex. These guys had great chemistry together and HOLY GOD was Rex <b>thorough</b> in the bedroom! ...and in the shower ...and against (multiple) trees. If you read this book and say that you don't want a bed partner as attentive as Rex, I'll call you a filthy liar. <br /><br />* how central the relationship between Rex and Daniel was to the book - no extraneous bullshit, no melodrama, just two guys struggling and falling in love at a realistic pace.<br /><br />* while being inside Daniel's head for the entire novel could get a bit wearing at times, I really enjoy watching the growth of his character over the course of the book; I felt like it was two steps forward, and one step back, so that the eventual growth and happiness felt hard won and well-deserved. <br /><br />* Ginger - I liked her caring, take-no-prisoners approach to life<br /><br />What I didn't enjoy so much:<br /><br />* the book was FAR too long and I felt like this hurt the story's pacing. This was a story that could have easily been told in 300 pages instead of 370. <br /><br />* first person, present tense isn't a favourite of mine. I get that this is a stylistic choice and that it's the way that the author felt comfortable writing, but as a reader, I found myself physically cringing for the first few pages until I relax into it a little bit... <br /><br />* the fact that the epilogue focused on Daniel and Ginger. I really wish that the books had finished with our two main characters in a room, together and happy. In fact, if Parrish had ended things after the Christmas present exchange - when Daniel is looking around the cabin and thinking that life is pretty much perfect - I would have been blissfully happy.<br /><br />* the set up for Colin's book. I really don't care to read about that d-bag. Leo and Will, on the other hand? I'm looking forward to it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18343944061970509797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1322680160" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8168524814403415530">Reread October 2016<br/><br/>Original review:<br/>4.5 stars!<br/><br/>I was worried. For two reasons. First - the hype. When there's a lot of hype, it's easier to be let down. Second - Daniel came across as a tad exhausting in the first few chapters. But I needn't have worried.<br/><br/>This is the debut novel of Roan Parrish and bravo! This story is <b>simple</b> perfection. There is no suspense, murder, mystery, police, etc. And that was the perfection of it. It was just a love story. And I ate that shit up!!!!<br/><br/>Daniel moves to the midd</span>
  <span id="freeText8168524814403415530" style="display:none">Reread October 2016<br /><br />Original review:<br />4.5 stars!<br /><br />I was worried. For two reasons. First - the hype. When there's a lot of hype, it's easier to be let down. Second - Daniel came across as a tad exhausting in the first few chapters. But I needn't have worried.<br /><br />This is the debut novel of Roan Parrish and bravo! This story is <b>simple</b> perfection. There is no suspense, murder, mystery, police, etc. And that was the perfection of it. It was just a love story. And I ate that shit up!!!!<br /><br />Daniel moves to the middle of Bumfuck, Nowhere for a job and meets Rex in this sleepy little town. The whole story is THEM! And the length...I am a book-length whore. The longer the better (usually), and especially when I'm enjoying a story. This was 350 pages of yummy goodness! The pacing was perfect - it never felt too long or rushed in any word.<br /><br />The simplicity was everything here, guys. I can't explain it any better than that. The way Parrish writes was so poignant in places that I found myself rereading paragraphs and dialogue because it was so well-stated. It was just SUCH a beautiful love story. Told entirely from Daniel's POV, but I never once felt like I didn't know exactly what was going on with Rex after the first quarter. And the steam? Holy shit. It was HAWT, but so touching too because of the writing. It was woven so perfectly with the couple themselves. <br /><br />I will definitely be looking out for this author in the future. Like I said, it's not a story that will knock your socks off because of all the "happenings" but it will stay with you for a while, nonetheless. I will definitely be rereading this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8168524814403415530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16915723647522603313">Rex, take me! Seriously, because I am in love with you! <br/><br/>I'm assuming there will be a second book because I really want more regarding some things that were left open ended.<br/><br/>That being said, I really enjoyed this one. I loved the relationships between Daniel/Ginger, Daniel/Leo, and Daniel/Will. Daniel is a hard one to figure out.   <span id="freeText16915723647522603313" style="display:none">Rex, take me! Seriously, because I am in love with you! <br /><br />I'm assuming there will be a second book because I really want more regarding some things that were left open ended.<br /><br />That being said, I really enjoyed this one.               <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8215520-adam?shelf=wrote-a-review">wrote-a-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8215520-adam?shelf=broken-boys">broken-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8215520-adam?shelf=disability-illness-injury-etc">disability-illness-injury-etc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8215520-adam?shelf=mm-contemporary">mm-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8215520-adam?shelf=toppy-alpha-top">toppy-alpha-top</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1321108464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17653173590820984774">First, let's take a moment to appreciate that book cover.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437019680ra/15528683.gif' width='300px' height='300px' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Now wipe that drool off your chin.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421946403ra/13433230.gif' width='350px' height='220px' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>Given that insanely hot cover, an interesting blurb, and the raving pre-release reviews, I was stoked to read 'In the Middle of Somewhere'. While I enjoyed it overall, it wasn't exactly the 4 or 5 star read I was hoping it would be.<br/><br/>I loved the small-town setting. The town of Holiday, Michigan, is off the beaten track, held in place perhaps only because of the small local college. I've developed a fondness </span>
  <span id="freeText17653173590820984774" style="display:none">First, let's take a moment to appreciate that book cover.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437019680ra/15528683.gif" width="300px" height="300px" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now wipe that drool off your chin.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421946403ra/13433230.gif" width="350px" height="220px" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Given that insanely hot cover, an interesting blurb, and the raving pre-release reviews, I was stoked to read 'In the Middle of Somewhere'. While I enjoyed it overall, it wasn't exactly the 4 or 5 star read I was hoping it would be.<br><br>I loved the small-town setting. The town of Holiday, Michigan, is off the beaten track, held in place perhaps only because of the small local college. I've developed a fondness for small-town romances in the past year or so. So Holiday was right up my alley. There's town gossip, family-owned businesses, everything is within walking distance, and it's all surrounded by forests. My inner sap was very pleased.<br><br>But you know what made my inner sap really jump for joy? Rex! He embodied the words 'husband material'. It's possible he was a bit <i>too</i> perfect, but I'm not complaining. The man is sweet, caring, hard-working, and incredibly sexy. If he ever comes to life, I call dibs. So, the romantic setting and the irresistible love interest made for a really good story.<br><br>What knocked this book down a star was the POV. The book is told from Daniel's perspective. While I liked it at first, I became increasingly bored in the second half. Daniel's running, and repetitive, inner monologues were annoying. He went from being edgy, to being a bit of whiner. <br><br>I think the main problem was that this book is too long for the story it's telling. A low-drama and fairly low-angst romance doesn't need these many pages, and stretching it out meant that repetition was bound to happen. 300 pages, if not less, would have been more than enough to tell Daniel and Rex's love story.<br><br>So 3 stars from me. I liked it and for the first two-thirds this book was 4 stars, but after that I was just waiting for the end. I'd recommend 'In the Middle of Somewhere' for MM readers who like a long slow-paced romance. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17653173590820984774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12651944735838539012" style="display:none">I mean, basically all my three stars are because Rex was amazing. But the book was so looooong.           <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14879044-elsbeth?shelf=m-m-romance-fiction">m-m-romance-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14879044-elsbeth?shelf=worth-rereading">worth-rereading</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1321517248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9056810035768136506"><br/><b>BR, July 11th with Susan and Julie</b><br/><br/>I really, really loved this book!!! It was beautiful ♡♡♡<br/><br/>This is a story focused mainly on the character developments… <br/><br/>Daniel Mulligan is the youngest of a family of boys. All his brothers and father care about is cars and sports.. Daniel has always been the outcast because of being gay and wanting different in his life. He graduates from college and needs a job saving money to continue his career.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Daniel</u>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436985985i/15525606._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='500' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>He is interviewed for this job as a English professor at</span>
  <span id="freeText9056810035768136506" style="display:none"><br><b>BR, July 11th with Susan and Julie</b><br><br>I really, really loved this book!!! It was beautiful ♡♡♡<br><br>This is a story focused mainly on the character developments… <br><br>Daniel Mulligan is the youngest of a family of boys. All his brothers and father care about is cars and sports.. Daniel has always been the outcast because of being gay and wanting different in his life. He graduates from college and needs a job saving money to continue his career.<br><br><b>
  <u>Daniel</u>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436985985i/15525606._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He is interviewed for this job as a English professor at a college in a small town in Michigan. Driving back home he hits a dog and after he goes searching for help it is where he meets Rex Vale. Rex takes him home, offers him food, a shower and a bed. After some kissing, Daniel finds himself alone in the cottage the next morning.<br><br>After 6 months, Daniel returns to the town Holiday. He is offered the position at the college. <br><br>He has not been able to get Rex out of his mind. Of course their pathes meet again and their reunion “ends” up against a tree.. This is the beginning of a slow progression of their relationship.<br><br>Their sex encounters were scorching hot!! I have never read anything like that.. I adored Rex in worshipping Daniel’s body and soul!!!<br><br>I loved that there was no angst other than Rex being worried about Daniel leaving him because everyone always left him.<br><br><b>
  <u>Rex</u>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436985985i/15525607.jpg" width="400" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"All I can hear is what Will just told me and Rex saying he can help me. It’s like there’s a screaming in my head that is Rex pulling the gate down, just like Will said."<br><br>“Please don’t be all helpful!” I blurt out. “Don’t slam the fucking gate down and pull away!”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428430215i/14421605.jpg" width="400" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No unnecessary misunderstandings.They were able to talk things out like grownups quite quickly. The only thing I missed a bit was Rex’s POV cause I really wanted to get in his mind… Boy, I would really like a boyfriend like him….<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436985985i/15525608.jpg" width="300" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Live with me. Here, for now. Then, wherever. As long as you’re with me, I won’t care where we live.” <br><br>“I can build something else. Something just for us.”<br><br>“I came here because I didn’t have anywhere else to go. Didn’t have anyone. And now…. As long as I’m with you, I’ll be home.”</i>
  </b>
