<div id="review_1321507364" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1321507364" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1088245-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359727841p2/1088245.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1321507364?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/1088245-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781634762120" href="/book/show/25687508-in-the-middle-of-somewhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1088245-debra?shelf=bad-parenting">bad-parenting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1088245-debra?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1088245-debra?shelf=arcs-and-for-review">arcs-and-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1088245-debra?shelf=part-of-series-or-serial">part-of-series-or-serial</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1088245-debra?shelf=teachers">teachers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1088245-debra?shelf=reviewed-for-sinfully">reviewed-for-sinfully</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1321507364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2219059183833559529"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Tough, tattooed, city boy Daniel finds himself in the middle of nowhere northern Michigan interviewing for a job as an English professor at small Sleeping Bear liberal arts college. While the interview goes well, the return trip to his hotel does not and he soon finds his car crashing into a tree to avoid hitting a dog. Rex, a shy, carpenter who is built like a god and, according to Daniel may or may not be a serial killer, appears from the woods to offer his assistance and brings both </span>
  <span id="freeText2219059183833559529" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />Tough, tattooed, city boy Daniel finds himself in the middle of nowhere northern Michigan interviewing for a job as an English professor at small Sleeping Bear liberal arts college. While the interview goes well, the return trip to his hotel does not and he soon finds his car crashing into a tree to avoid hitting a dog. Rex, a shy, carpenter who is built like a god and, according to Daniel may or may not be a serial killer, appears from the woods to offer his assistance and brings both Daniel and the dog to his cabin in the woods. Not the greatest of first meetings, but Daniel is drawn to the intense Rex against his better judgment and spends the evening at the cabin. One thing leads to another, the two men share a kiss, but Daniel wakes up to an empty house. Flash forward six months and Daniel is on his way to start his new job in Michigan and worrying about possibly running into Rex again, but really hoping he does.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this novel. It was so well written, with great dialogue, I can’t believe it’s the author’s first book! The relationship between the men starts off slowly, but it is quickly apparent the two opposites are just what the other needs. The sexual chemistry is undeniable, but both men are fumbling when it comes to the other parts of having a relationship. As Daniel is trying to settle into his new life, there is still the possibility that he will be moving on if a job at another school opens up in his area of expertise. Rex is a talented carpenter, with a penchant for old movies, but at times feels like he isn’t good enough to keep up with Daniel’s education and intellect and has a fear of losing yet another person he cares for. As their relationship slowly progresses they deal with jealousies and misunderstandings while trying to navigate the minefields of their pasts, one of which comes to a head when Daniel suddenly needs to return home to Philadelphia and Rex goes with him.<br /><br />There are some great secondary characters including Daniel’s best friend Ginger, Leo (who is apparently a young Daniel), Rex’s best friend Will and even Daniel’s hateful brothers and apathetic father. I am glad to see this is a first in a planned series of books. There is no cliffhanger here, but there are definitely some story lines that have more to them for both the main and secondary characters. I’m definitely looking to read more from Roan Parrish in the future. <br /><br /><b>Review originally posted at <a href="http://sinfullysexybooks.blogspot.co.uk/2015/07/release-day-review-in-middle-of.html#more" rel="nofollow noopener">Sinfully...Addicted to All Male Romance</a>. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2219059183833559529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1457131077" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1457131077" />
    <a title="Meep" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6273941-meep"><img alt="Meep" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331477806p2/6273941.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1457131077?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meep" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meep" href="/user/show/6273941-meep">Meep</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25862832-in-the-middle-of-somewhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6273941-meep?shelf=favourite">favourite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6273941-meep?shelf=have-audio">have-audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1457131077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15156232307605981198">Re-read - I still like the book but Daniel is a bit much in comparison to Rex's solid calm and Ginger is FAR too omniscient, her name is mentioned 306 through the book, the epilogue consolidates this as the Ginger-Daniel show which kills the romantic vibe.<br/><br/>-- --<br/>Audio for this is very engaging too.<br/>None of the voices felt forced and there's the right amount of expression.<br/><br/>-- --<br/>Lets just accept Rex is the perfect (fictional) man and move on ;)<br/>Seriously though; big strong, handsome, skilled with his h</span>
  <span id="freeText15156232307605981198" style="display:none">Re-read - I still like the book but Daniel is a bit much in comparison to Rex's solid calm and Ginger is FAR too omniscient, her name is mentioned 306 through the book, the epilogue consolidates this as the Ginger-Daniel show which kills the romantic vibe.<br /><br />-- --<br />Audio for this is very engaging too.<br />None of the voices felt forced and there's the right amount of expression.<br /><br />-- --<br />Lets just accept Rex is the perfect (fictional) man and move on ;)<br />Seriously though; big strong, handsome, skilled with his hands, <i>skilled with his hands</i>, big heart, big <i>everything</i>, gentle, caring, protective, built own cabin, saved cute doggy, really sees people. Yum. Thorough in the bedroom (and in showers, and against trees..) And his sex talk, hot damn!<br /><br />Daniel while I liked the -poor, sexy, hard-working, inked, professor- he needed to get over himself at times; a big part of that is the choice of first person, present tense. I struggled with the first pages then settled into the flow but it's not a favourite pov choice for a long fic and wont suit everyone. Here it meant too much time mired in Daniel's insecurities. Realistic progress, but it did make the story feel repetitive at times.<br /><br />Ginger though barely present is somewhat omniscient. She's great, a very colourful character, but leave the little chick outta the nest already, he's a grown arsed professor now! I both loved her and wanted to hear less from her! I liked Leo and Will.<br /><br />It's a long slow story; at what felt like halfway I realised I was only at 12%! But I very much enjoyed the slow getting to know each other and building trust, more about Daniel coming to terms with himself than any outside issues, almost a coming of age story. The focus is very much on the main couple, there's a warm feel whenever the two get together. Insta-attraction but feelings are far more complicated and slow to be defined. Enjoyable watching them get to know each other and seeing how well they fit together. I was happy the whole time reading.<br /><br />There's some drama after the 70% mark, I'm not convinced we needed that, or Daniel's resulting monologue. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[it seemed an excuse to get him back to Philly and introduce Rex to the douchery of his 'family' <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I kind of resented the intrusion of Colin's issues there at the end (although I'm curious about his book). Also could have done without the epilogue; the story actually ends at a really good moment, then the epilogue dilutes that and turns the end feels more to Daniel-Ginger than Daniel-Rex as it should be. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And while I love the 'home is with you' vibe got to admit I'll be disappointed if they leave the cabin, wish that part had been decided. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's a mix of these things late in the story that stole a star, and I'm still debating adding it.<br /><br />Had a few niggles, none of consequence;<br />-Windows being painted shut mentioned twice at length (stuffy, no air con., carbon monoxide risk...) then later he leaves his window open a crack to air out his room. <br />-There's a snow storm but next morning Daniel is prepared to walk home with no reference to snow, then or for several chapters.<br />-The repeated 'people judge me for my tatts' - boo-hoo, own them, love them, or don't get them!<br />-Nightmares that came from nowhere; them and their conflict revealed then forgotten in a page. <br /><br />But overall a really impressive debut book and one I will re-read. I look forward to the sequel, it's going to be interesting to see how such a negatively portrayed character can become sympathetic. I'm expecting some angsty conflict and hope the emotions are explored. An author I'll be looking out for.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15156232307605981198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1322176981" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1322176981" />
    <a title="Kaje Harper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5309738-kaje-harper"><img alt="Kaje Harper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307630447p2/5309738.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1322176981?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaje Harper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaje Harper" href="/user/show/5309738-kaje-harper">Kaje Harper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781634762120" href="/book/show/25687508-in-the-middle-of-somewhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309738-kaje-harper?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309738-kaje-harper?shelf=signif-past-abuse">signif-past-abuse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1322176981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10246007746955563072">Daniel is a tough Philly kid who grew up to be an English professor, despite the obstacles of no money, and a blue-collar father and brothers who have only disdain for any kind of education, and who hate the fact that Daniel is gay. Despite being estranged from his family, he loves the big city. But the only job he's offered after graduate school is in the wilds of rural Michigan, and he takes it out of necessity, hoping something better will come along.<br/><br/>And there he meets Rex, a quiet, large and</span>
  <span id="freeText10246007746955563072" style="display:none">Daniel is a tough Philly kid who grew up to be an English professor, despite the obstacles of no money, and a blue-collar father and brothers who have only disdain for any kind of education, and who hate the fact that Daniel is gay. Despite being estranged from his family, he loves the big city. But the only job he's offered after graduate school is in the wilds of rural Michigan, and he takes it out of necessity, hoping something better will come along.<br /><br />And there he meets Rex, a quiet, large and gentle man who has an astounding tolerance for Daniel's gun-shy reactions, smart mouth, pessimistic outlook and big-city ways. This is a true meeting of opposites, and while Daniel is eagerly hoping for the greener pastures of a big-city job, he may be missing the best thing that could happen to him.<br /><br />I really enjoyed Daniel. He's well drawn as a guy who has never had any support for anything he wants to do, and assumes he's always in for a fight. He has one good friend back in Philly, but is otherwise alone and he constantly expects to be judged for everything he does and says. He has the ability be a friend and to love, but it's buried under a lot of defensive layers. <br /><br />Rex is a little bit too good to be true - a big sweet bear of a guy who cooks, cares, and is excellent in bed. But he's a good foil for Daniel's prickly nature, and, with the height of the walls Daniel has surrounded himself with (and the sharpness of the razor wire of his sometimes-thoughtless comments that tops them), he needs someone this good. They are sweet together, and the sex is hot (although perhaps a little plentiful.) Rex has his flaws too, although they are mainly sympathetic ones.<br /><br />This book gets better as it goes along. The emotional crisis moment made me start to really enjoy the story to the full. I did hit a few small pet peeves. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Saying "I'm clean" in place of test results, for example. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And at times I felt pulled out of the moment by the present-tense narration, especially when switching from a past event back to the main story thread. But in general it's well-written, and the characters are engaging (and the strongest part of the book). I would read another novel from this author, and this story left some room open for either direct or other-character sequels. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10246007746955563072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1312014078" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1312014078" />
    <a title="Ele" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22695216-ele"><img alt="Ele" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523264242p2/22695216.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1312014078?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ele" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ele" href="/user/show/22695216-ele">Ele</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25862832-in-the-middle-of-somewhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22695216-ele?shelf=hottest-man-on-man-action">hottest-man-on-man-action</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1312014078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14723700354642458887"><b>*3.5 stars*<br/><br/>Impressive debut novel from Roan Parrish! I'm honest when I say that I wouldn't have guessed this is a new author's work</b><br/><br/>Apart from the solid writing there were many things I liked:<br/>-<b>Rex.</b>Who in their right mind wouldn't like Rex? The man was the perfect boyfriend, or maybe the perfect human being!<br/>-<b>The sex.</b> Every sex scene in this story is very emotional. It is never just sex, these men have amazing chemistry and a deep connection. And although scorching hot and filthy, the sex doesn't t</span>
  <span id="freeText14723700354642458887" style="display:none"><b>*3.5 stars*<br /><br />Impressive debut novel from Roan Parrish! I'm honest when I say that I wouldn't have guessed this is a new author's work</b><br /><br />Apart from the solid writing there were many things I liked:<br />-<b>Rex.</b>Who in their right mind wouldn't like Rex? The man was the perfect boyfriend, or maybe the perfect human being!<br />-<b>The sex.</b> Every sex scene in this story is very emotional. It is never just sex, these men have amazing chemistry and a deep connection. And although scorching hot and filthy, the sex doesn't take over (which is what I expected because of the length of the book).<br />-<b> No small town drama.</b> Yes, there are some bigoted assholes, as expected, but homophobia is not a theme here. People are pretty accepting and actually very likeable characters.<br />-<b>Unexpected funny moments.</b>Like Marjorie at the cafe, naming an espresso after Daniel.<br /><br />But, I have to admit that while there were many 5 star parts in this book, there were others that made me struggle a little bit.<br /><b>My main niggle is that it is too long.</b> I don't have a problem with stories entirely focused on the couple, on the contrary I like them. But it could be shorter. And because we only get Daniel's POV it got a bit repetitive. I did like Daniel and I understand where he was coming from. But man, being in his head for so long was exhausting.<br /><b>Ginger.</b>Don't shoot! I know everybody likes her. I liked her too. But why <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[did it have to be Daniel and Ginger in the end, instead of Daniel and Rex? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I had enough of her through the story, she practically lived inside Daniel's head. He almost never acted before thinking what Ginger would have said.<br /><br />Despite the above, I liked the story and I will definately be reading the next books in the series. I particularly want to read Collin's story (yeah yeah I know, you want to punch him in the throat, I do too)<br /><br />Cudos to the author!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14723700354642458887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1474244731" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1474244731" />
    <a title="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower"><img alt="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467816536p2/29402776.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1474244731?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" href="/user/show/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower">The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781634762120" href="/book/show/25687508-in-the-middle-of-somewhere">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower?shelf=m-m-g-contemporary">m-m-g-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower?shelf=m-m-p-teacher-scholar">m-m-p-teacher-scholar</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower?shelf=m-m-4-stars">m-m-4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower?shelf=m-m-p-blue-collar">m-m-p-blue-collar</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower?shelf=m-m-sc-versatile">m-m-sc-versatile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower?shelf=m-m-series">m-m-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower?shelf=m-m-l-long">m-m-l-long</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower?shelf=m-m-t-alpha-males">m-m-t-alpha-males</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1474244731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10096587823559260191"><i>In the Middle of Somewhere</i> was a very <b>entertaining contemporary read</b> with <b>catching main characters</b>. <br/><br/><b>Daniel</b> is used to live in a big city, but when applying for a job at a small school in <b>Michigan</b>, he finds himself in the middle of nowhere. His first trip to Holiday ends in a disaster - hitting a dog during a car crash he is lost in the woods and feels completely helpless. When <b>Rex</b> - a shy and withdrawn carpenter - finds and takes him to his cabin to help the dog, they immediately feel attrackted</span>
  <span id="freeText10096587823559260191" style="display:none"><i>In the Middle of Somewhere</i> was a very <b>entertaining contemporary read</b> with <b>catching main characters</b>. <br /><br /><b>Daniel</b> is used to live in a big city, but when applying for a job at a small school in <b>Michigan</b>, he finds himself in the middle of nowhere. His first trip to Holiday ends in a disaster - hitting a dog during a car crash he is lost in the woods and feels completely helpless. When <b>Rex</b> - a shy and withdrawn carpenter - finds and takes him to his cabin to help the dog, they immediately feel attrackted to each other. Unfortunatley, the both have their issues and don't know how to act around each other. They slowly figure out how to be in a relationship and are getting closer to each other. When all of a sudden terrible news from home reach Daniel, he is about to fact one of the most difficult episodes of his life. But compared to all other times, he isn't alone in this one. <br /><br />The whole story is told out of <b>Daniel's POV</b> and we thus get his sometimes confusing thoughts and all his insecurities. I really liked him as a characters, but I somehow had the feeling that I didn't get as close to Rex. He is a very interesting character and I guess that there is a lot more about him that we still don't know. It would have been great to get a few scenes from his POV. <br /><br />I enjoyed Roan Parrish's <b>writing style</b> a lot. With every page I was able to discover more about Daniel and Rex. It took me some time to figure out how they feel and what makes them react they way they did. But with every <b>secret revealed</b> the pieces of the puzzle slowly came together and I started to feel closer and closer to the main characters. They were very well sketched and the character development felt very credible. <br /><br /><i>In the Middle of Somewhere</i> has a <b>solid and catching plot</b> without having any over-the-top drama. This story could definitely happen in <b>real life</b>. Roan Parrish managed to tie all the loose ends while leaving enough room for imagination. A few questions stayed unanswered and I'm really looking forward to the second part of this series. <br /><br />The <b>secondary characters</b> were great - I espacially loved Ginger and Leo. They all had their own story and I loved reading all the scenes featuring one or more of them. I'm super curious to find out if one of the upcoming books will be about Leo and Will. I'm also looking forward to read more about Daniel's brother Colin. <br /><br />The pace of the story was ok, some episodes felt a bit <b>too long</b>. I guess it would have been a five star read, if the pace had been a little more balanced. <br /><br /><b>4 stars!</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="10096587823559260191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3619419761292918394"><b><br/>First Read 7/2015<br/>Second Read 2/2016</b><br/><br/><br/>It took be a while to think of a rating and a review for this book. I want to say first that for a debut book this author nailed it. She did a great job with the characters and the story line. I enjoyed her writing style alot. She wrote the perfect guy in my eyes. I love Rex, everything about him. I have no bad words for him, I thoroughly enjoyed his character from start to finish. I understand him more that it's been 2 days since I've finished the book.   <span id="freeText3619419761292918394" style="display:none"><b><br />First Read 7/2015<br />Second Read 2/2016</b><br /><br /><br />It took be a while to think of a rating and a review for this book. I want to say first that for a debut book this author nailed it. She did a great job with the characters and the story line. I enjoyed her writing style alot. She wrote the perfect guy in my eyes. I love Rex, everything about him. I have no bad words for him, I thoroughly enjoyed his character from start to finish. I understand him more that it's been 2 days since I've finished the book. I get that he enjoys the simple things in life, and people. Sure I wanted to throttle him a few times, but he made up for all the little things he did. The internet, the food, the listening, and just being Rex. I want me a Rex now!!! <br /><br />Now let's get to Daniel. Daniel was a lost boy if anybody else was. Gah for all his pigheadedness, I still loved him. I kinda felt sorry felt sorry for him, because he did not know love it seemed like. I don't know if that is true, but from what I seen he was lacking love outside of Ginger. Goodness his brothers were a class act. Ugh I wanted to rip their entails out. Ummm weren't they born and bred in Philadelphia? Isn't that the "City of Brotherly Love" Not really! Ugh I hated his entire family. It's not going to change since I've finished the book. I really liked how the author did the supporting characters, Leo &amp; Will, I liked both of those guys.<br /><br />Why not 5 stars? Well sometimes Daniel inner voice got on my nerves. It was too much at times. I wanted him to have a little confidence of his own, I wanted him to man up at times, and sure he did it, but by then I was over it. I get why he needed the reassurances, but I sometimes just wanted him to spontaneous do something. I wanted him to put himself out there a little bit more. This might be minor to some people, but it was a problem for me. I can't wait to see more from this author. I thank her for giving us these wonderful characters.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1334103249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10027860034302638723">I was in the middle of writing a long ass review of this book when I decided to look something up in another tab. When I went back to my review tab Safari decides to auto refresh, which seems to happen a lot on iPads whether they're new or not. Sooooo I'll just write a short one.<br/><br/>I liked quite a lot of things about this book. I liked that Daniel had flaws and could be annoying. I liked that it was long and meandering. I liked Ginger, I loved Rex (even if he was a bit too perfect). I liked that Da</span>
  <span id="freeText10027860034302638723" style="display:none">I was in the middle of writing a long ass review of this book when I decided to look something up in another tab. When I went back to my review tab Safari decides to auto refresh, which seems to happen a lot on iPads whether they're new or not. Sooooo I'll just write a short one.<br /><br />I liked quite a lot of things about this book. I liked that Daniel had flaws and could be annoying. I liked that it was long and meandering. I liked Ginger, I loved Rex (even if he was a bit too perfect). I liked that Daniel's brothers were assholes because they were pretty realistic for where he was from. I especially liked that there was not this dual POV business that seems to be the rage right now. I don't usually want to know what the other characters are thinking so this was extra refreshing. I liked that it was long and meandering. I think a lot of authors in this genre are forced to cut their books very short or write only a certain amount of words, and it's usually pretty obvious in the way that the endings seem super rushed and tacked on. <br /><br />I STRONGLY disliked the repetitous words and phrases, especially during the sex scenes. Using words like "heat" 65 times (yes I counted) as a euphemism for a certain body part is not cute. Neither is "channel". It's also not cute to have a pretty pragmatic story broken up by quasi poetic descriptors during sex scenes, even if the sex scenes were pretty damned hot. I don't like feeling the need to laugh because of both of those issues during those scenes. I was also bothered by the fact that some of the positions didn't make any sense as they were described. See this review for some examples of what I'm talking about: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1303280236?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a>. <br /><br />I also didn't like that Daniel seemed very... I was going to say girlish but maybe the word I'm looking for is young. There was a lot of Rex picking Daniel up and Daniel sitting on Rex's lap and more things that kind of rubbed me the wrong way. It just seemed odd. To be honest, I didn't even realize that Daniel was supposed to be 30 until I read it in a review. <br /><br />Lastly, first person can be awkward and it's not always the best choice for a story, especially a long one. <br /><br />Kudos to the author for having an ending that is HEA but not ridiculously so, and for having an epilogue that's not focused on the main couple. That was a refreshing change.<br /><br />I do think a really good editor could have made this book into a 5 star read, but it was still highly enjoyable regardless of its flaws. I think this is one book that many people will either end up loving or hating with very few middle of the road reactions. I am looking forward to reading about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Daniel's brother Colin in another book because that should be super interesting. I want to know what made him push his brother away so hard, even though I did guess he was gay long before the big reveal. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="10027860034302638723" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('J+L9a1vfAp46s4vfYbDWweN2EI+yT8jTHHYtty/7fk+ad7vQ92hrgAEvjNwFdOk/fe+krJmExwDDM6SdVfzrzA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('j/sag1PjchNWbNMTQxZT0eB0eP6BqxY5XiA98dcYLXMyblw4/1QbDW3w1BAn0mwvfu3M3apgGeqBZbTbrR+48A==')})
  }
//]]>

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_34928609'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34928609-heart-of-the-steal?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Heart of the Steal<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/14237686.Avon_Gale?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Avon Gale<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.84 avg rating &mdash; 1,193 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2017\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer15320796304465281697\">Responsible, disciplined William Fox channeled his love for art and his faith in the rules into being an FBI Art Crimes agent. Right and wrong, justice and injustice—the differences are clear, and Will has spent his career drawing a line between them<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText15320796304465281697\" style=\"display:none\">Responsible, disciplined William Fox channeled his love for art and his faith in the rules into being an FBI Art Crimes agent. Right and wrong, justice and injustice—the differences are clear, and Will has spent his career drawing a line between them. Maybe his convictions have cost him relationships, but he’s not willing to compromise what he knows is right. Until the night he meets Amory Vaughn.\n\nAs the head of his family’s philanthropic foundation, Vaughn knows very well that being rich and powerful can get him almost anything he wants. And when he meets endearingly grumpy and slightly awkward William Fox, he wants him more than he’s wanted anything. Vaughn is used to being desired for his name and his money, but Will doesn’t care about either.\n\nWhen Vaughn falls back on old habits and attempts to impress Will by stealing a painting Will admires, their nascent bond blows up in his face. But Vaughn isn’t willing to give up on the glimpse of passion he saw the night he took Will apart. Before Will knows it, he’s falling for the man he should have arrested, and Vaughn has to realize that some things can’t be bought or stolen. Love has to be given freely. But can a man who lives by the rules, and a man who thinks the rules don’t apply to him, ever see eye to eye? \n\n\nHeart of the Steal is a standalone romance with a happy ending. It features a Southern gentleman who thinks he’s always right, a buttoned-up FBI agent who secretly likes his buttons unbuttoned, and wall sex. And desk sex. <span id="freeTextContainer435575343556590521">Roan Parrish lives in Philadelphia, where she is gradually attempting to write love stories in every genre.<br/><br/>When not writing, she can usually be found cutting her friends’ hair, meandering through whatever city she’s in while listening to torch songs and melodic death metal, or cooking overly elaborate meals. She loves bonfires, winter beaches, minor chord harmonies, and self-tattooing. One time sh</span>
  <span id="freeText435575343556590521" style="display:none">Roan Parrish lives in Philadelphia, where she is gradually attempting to write love stories in every genre.<br /><br />When not writing, she can usually be found cutting her friends’ hair, meandering through whatever city she’s in while listening to torch songs and melodic death metal, or cooking overly elaborate meals. She loves bonfires, winter beaches, minor chord harmonies, and self-tattooing. One time she may or may not have baked a six-layer chocolate cake and then thrown it out the window in a fit of pique.<br /><br />She is represented by Courtney Miller-Callihan of Handspun Literary Agency.<br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/2xHGvBj" rel="nofollow noopener">Roan's Newsletter</a><br /><a href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/parrishorperish/" rel="nofollow noopener">Roan's Facebook Group</a><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/RoanParrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Roan on Twitter</a><br /><a href="https://instagram.com/roanparrish/" rel="nofollow noopener">Roan on Instagram</a><br /><a href="http://roanparrish.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Roan’s website</a></span>
